The probability overlay shows what expert players compute mentally: given the constraints, what is P(mine) for each hidden cell? Cells at 0% are safe clicks; cells at 100% are definite mines. The gray zone in between is where Minesweeper becomes genuinely hard — and NP-complete.

**Era 4-7** — 4-7 (Expert Boom → Generative-Agentic — game theory, imperfect information, Nash equilibrium)
- `HYB-006 liarsdice` — Liar's Dice requires modeling opponent beliefs about your beliefs — theory of mind. Nash equilibrium strategies exist but humans play with psychology. The same imperfect-information game theory powers poker AI (Libratus, Pluribus). Bluffing IS adversarial deception — the social equivalent of adversarial examples in ML.
- `HYB-015 liarsdice-bluff` — Liar's Dice is a game of incomplete information — you know your own dice but not your opponent's. Every bid is a claim about the total distribution across ALL dice. The bluff detector overlay computes the exact binomial probability that a bid is true, given what you can see. This transforms gut-feel bluffing into a mathematics lesson: when P(bid true) drops below 50%, calling "Liar!" becomes the optimal play. The overlay reveals the hidden math that skilled players compute intuitively.
- `SIM-012 antfarm` — Populous invented indirect control: modify the environment, let agents self-organize. The overlay reveals what makes emergence work — each agent's FSM state, need priorities, and social connections. This is exactly what Stanford's Generative Agents paper (2023) visualized: autonomous entities with internal state that produce emergent behavior. Molyneux built it in 1989; AI formalized it in 2023.

**Era 5** — 5 (Emergent Complexity — procedural worlds, player-driven meaning-making)
- `ADV-015 dream-walk` — Yume Nikki is an anti-game — it strips away objectives, scores, enemies, and dialogue to leave pure exploration. The player constructs meaning from surreal juxtapositions. This mirrors unsupervised learning: the system (player) finds patterns and clusters in unlabeled data (dream imagery) without explicit reward signals.
- `FGT-006 teeworlds` — Teeworlds' grappling hook transformed 2D combat from platform-hopping to physics-based acrobatics. The hook creates a continuous action space for movement — exactly the kind of high-dimensional control problem that deep reinforcement learning excels at but rule-based AI struggles with.
- `FIX-005 pop-defense` — Tower defense games are constraint satisfaction puzzles in real-time clothing. The optimal placement of fixed-position agents to intercept moving targets along known paths is equivalent to the facility location problem in operations research — NP-hard in general but approximable through greedy heuristics.
- `FIX-006 tower-defense` — Kingdom Rush added the hero unit to tower defense, giving the player one mobile piece on an otherwise static board. This single controllable agent amid automated defenses mirrors the human-in-the-loop paradigm in AI systems — most decisions are automated, but critical interventions require human judgment.
- `MAZ-008 capturetheflag` — CTF requires agents to adopt roles (attacker, defender, support) and switch dynamically based on game state. This multi-agent coordination problem — where individual optimal play differs from team-optimal play — is a foundational challenge in cooperative AI research.
- `MAZ-015 spin-navigate` — Rotating stick navigation creates a unique constraint satisfaction problem where the agent must plan trajectories that account for periodic geometric transformations. The continuously rotating elongated hitbox turns simple pathfinding into a time-dependent spatial reasoning challenge.
- `MAZ-017 bomb-battle` — Balloon bombing requires planning multi-step traps — predicting opponent movement and cutting off escape routes. This combines real-time pathfinding with game-tree search, as each balloon placement reshapes the navigation graph. Korea's decade-long obsession with BnB created enormous datasets of human strategic play.
- `PLT-010 platform-hop` — Doodle Jump's infinite procedural generation solved the content problem by making each playthrough unique — a constraint-based generative approach that predated modern procedural generation research in deep learning.
- `PLT-011 gravity` — Gravity flipping replaces the jump arc (a continuous analog curve) with a binary state toggle (up/down). This dramatically simplifies the control space while creating equally complex level design challenges. The reduced action space makes VVVVVV an ideal testbed for RL agents — two gravity states times horizontal position is a tractable state space, yet the levels require precise timing that challenges both humans and algorithms.
- `PLT-014 roof-sprint` — Canabalt's radical reduction to a single input mirrors dimensionality reduction in deep learning — proving that stripping away all but one axis of control can create emergent depth from environmental complexity alone.
- `PUZ-006 rope-physics` — Cut the Rope proved that touch-native physics puzzles could achieve the depth of desktop games. Its rope simulation reduced complex physics to a single intuitive verb — cutting — making Newtonian mechanics accessible to anyone who can swipe a finger.
- `PUZ-011 match3` — Match-3 with cascading is a stochastic optimization problem. The player must evaluate swaps by their immediate match AND potential cascade chains. This is expectimax search with uncertainty — the same framework used in probabilistic AI planning. Candy Crush proved that this simple mechanic could generate billions in revenue through careful difficulty tuning.
- `PUZ-019 tangram` — Tangram is a geometric constraint satisfaction problem: 7 pieces must tile a region with zero gaps and zero overlap. This is equivalent to polygon packing — an NP-hard problem that computer vision and robotics solve for bin packing, nesting, and assembly planning.
- `PUZ-022 grow` — GROW is a combinatorial optimization puzzle where 8! = 40,320 permutations yield exactly one perfect solution. The interaction matrix creates a directed graph of dependencies — items boost others placed before them, creating chain reactions that reward systems thinking over brute force.
- `PUZ-023 cursor10` — Cursor*10 elegantly demonstrates self-cooperation through temporal replay — a concept that parallels multi-agent reinforcement learning where past policies become teammates. Each ghost cursor is essentially a frozen policy that the current agent must cooperate with, creating an emergent coordination problem.
- `PUZ-026 engare` — Engare bridges mathematical curves and artistic intuition. A point on a rotating circle traces an epicycloid — the same mathematics behind Islamic geometric patterns. The player learns parametric equations through spatial reasoning, discovering that beauty and math are the same thing.
- `PUZ-027 farsh` — Farsh transforms the simple act of unrolling a carpet into a spatial reasoning puzzle. Each carpet is a rigid body with fixed length — the player must mentally simulate unrolling sequences to construct viable paths, a constraint-propagation problem that mirrors how neural networks learn spatial transformations.
- `PUZ-028 munin` — Section rotation creates a combinatorial state space where each rotation changes connectivity. Unlike sliding puzzles where tiles translate, rotation fundamentally reshapes the topology — platforms become walls, gaps become bridges. The AI challenge is reasoning about how local rotations create global path connectivity.
- `PUZ-031 ring-shooter` — Puzz Loop pioneered the marble-chain mechanic that Zuma popularized. The AI challenge is path prediction — calculating where a shot ball will intersect a moving chain on a curved track, requiring real-time trajectory and collision math that early arcade hardware handled through clever approximation.
- `PUZ-036 star-click` — Hoshi Saga is a meta-puzzle: the player must first discover WHAT to do before doing it. This mirrors the exploration-exploitation tradeoff in reinforcement learning — each screen demands a fresh hypothesis about the interaction model.
- `PUZ-039 quizquiz` — QuizQuiz married trivia knowledge with competitive puzzle mechanics, creating a hybrid where intellectual speed becomes a weapon. Nexon's 1999 release pioneered the free-to-play business model that would reshape the entire games industry. The quiz-as-attack mechanic is a unique fusion — correct answers become offensive moves, transforming knowledge into competitive advantage.
- `SCR-010 bullethell` — Bullet hell demands real-time trajectory prediction for hundreds of simultaneous objects. The player must parse complex geometric patterns, predict convergence points, and find safe corridors — spatial reasoning under extreme time pressure. The tiny hitbox is a deliberate design choice that makes near-misses feel skillful rather than lucky, a form of difficulty calibration that AI difficulty research didn't formalize until decades later.
- `SHT-006 tactical` — Modern military shooters elevated enemy AI from simple patrol-and-chase to tactical behavior — seeking cover, flanking, coordinating attacks. This mirrors the shift from reactive to planning-based AI, where agents reason about spatial relationships and opponent state.
- `SHT-009 arc-artillery` — GunBound's vehicle selection meta-game layers strategic identity onto artillery physics. Each mobile creates a distinct problem space — the same wind and terrain demand different solutions depending on your vehicle. This mirrors ensemble methods in ML where different model architectures excel at different problem domains.
- `SIM-016 drill-mine` — Motherload distills the core loop of resource extraction games into its purest form — the downward journey as metaphor for increasing commitment. Each descent is a gamble: fuel is finite, minerals are uncertain, and the surface grows farther away. The game teaches sunk-cost reasoning through embodied experience.
- `SIM-020 territory-dice` — Dicewars reduces territorial strategy to pure probability. Each attack is a known distribution (sum of N dice vs sum of M dice). The optimal strategy balances risk-taking with preserving connected territory for bonus dice. AI must evaluate not just immediate win probability but downstream effects on territory connectivity — a graph theory problem wrapped in probability.
- `SPT-008 rhythm` — Rhythm games require precise temporal pattern matching — the player must predict when each note arrives and execute within a tight timing window. This is real-time sequence alignment, the same problem solved by dynamic time warping in speech recognition. The combo system rewards consistency, mirroring how statistical models reward sustained accuracy over lucky individual predictions.
- `SPT-010 darts` — Expert darts players exhibit motor precision under pressure. The optimal target depends on your accuracy: beginners should aim for the large 19/7 region, not triple-20. This is the explore-exploit tradeoff — play safe or gamble for high scores. The Kelly criterion from gambling theory applies directly.
- `SPT-017 nanacacrash` — Nanaca Crash went viral in Japan as a Flash game in 2005, pioneering the launch-and-bounce genre. The deceptive simplicity — two clicks to launch, then pray for good bounces — hides a genuine optimization problem: angle and power selection interact nonlinearly with random character placement to create enormous variance in outcomes.
- `SPT-024 golf-aim` — Pangya's three-click swing mechanic decomposes the continuous challenge of hitting a golf ball into three discrete timing decisions. Each click is a separate test of motor skill, turning a smooth analog action into a rhythm game. The 'Pangya!' perfect shot — requiring all three clicks in ideal zones — creates a Skinnerian variable-ratio reward schedule that drove Korea's PC bang addiction to the game.
- `SPT-025 rhythm-dance` — Audition Online separates the rhythm game into two cognitive phases: first memorize a sequence (working memory), then execute with precise timing (motor timing). This two-phase structure mirrors how statistical models handle sequence-to-sequence tasks — encode the input, then decode at the right moment. The combo length scaling tests working memory capacity, which in humans is famously limited to 7±2 items.
- `SPT-026 freestyle` — Freestyle's AI opponents used pattern recognition to predict player tendencies — if you always drove left, the AI would shade that direction. This created a rock-paper-scissors metagame where players had to vary their approach, mirroring how real basketball defenders study film.
- `SPT-027 dance-arrows` — Pump It Up's 5-panel diamond layout creates a fundamentally different combinatorial space than DDR's 4-panel cross. The center panel enables crossover patterns and spins impossible on 4 panels. Step chart design is a constraint satisfaction problem — patterns must be physically executable while maximizing musical expression.
- `TRP-005 onelevel` — Rule mutation games invert normal game design: the environment is constant, only the rules vary. This mirrors transfer learning in AI — same architecture, different task. Each stage is a new policy the player must discover through experimentation, paralleling reinforcement learning exploration.
- `WLD-004 linerider` — Line Rider is a physics sandbox where the player IS the level designer. The core loop — draw, simulate, observe, iterate — mirrors the scientific method. AI could optimize tracks but would miss the creative joy of experimentation.
- `ADV-018 globe-deduction` — Carmen Sandiego is a constraint satisfaction problem. Each clue eliminates suspects and destinations. The deduction overlay shows what a Bayesian reasoner computes: posterior probabilities over suspects and cities after each clue, revealing how logical elimination narrows the search space exponentially.
- `MAZ-019 snake-optimal` — Snake is secretly a Hamiltonian path problem. The safest strategy visits every cell exactly once — but finding Hamiltonian paths is NP-complete. Real-time play forces heuristic tradeoffs between shortest-path greed and long-term survival. The overlay makes this tension visible.
- `MAZ-024 bomb-blast` — The blast overlay reveals the hidden topology of danger. Experienced players internalize approximate blast zones, but chain reactions — where one balloon triggers another — create exponential complexity that even experts misjudge. The overlay externalizes this propagation graph, showing how a single balloon can cascade through a chain to threaten cells far beyond its own range.
- `PHY-011 space-rocks-predict` — Category 1 AI-native prototype. The overlay renders Newtonian trajectory prediction: every asteroid's future path is projected 2-3 seconds ahead as dotted lines, collision risk points are marked, and safe zones — regions no asteroid will occupy — are highlighted in green. Transforms a reflex game into a physics planning puzzle.
- `PHY-012 pinball-predict` — Category 1 AI-native prototype. The trajectory overlay renders what a physics-aware AI would compute each frame: the ball's future path through bumpers, walls, and flipper zones, with optimal flip timing highlighted. Same mechanics as PHY-005 — a predictive lens added on top.
- `PLT-027 sprint-timing` — Canabalt is a one-button game where the only decision is when to jump. The prediction overlay reveals what the player's brain does intuitively — estimating gap distances, projecting jump arcs at current speed, and assessing whether a gap is clearable. This turns implicit spatial reasoning into explicit numerical prediction.
- `PUZ-042 ring-chain` — Puzz Loop becomes a planning game when you can see the future. The overlay uses graph connectivity analysis to predict not just immediate matches but the cascade of gap closures and secondary matches — turning reactive shooting into deliberate strategy.
- `PUZ-045 grow-optimal` — GROW's charm hides a combinatorial puzzle — 6 items yield 720 possible orderings, but only one maximizes all synergies. The optimization overlay reveals the interaction matrix that determines which items boost which others, turning trial-and-error into informed strategy. This is constraint satisfaction made visible.
- `PUZ-046 tangram-fit` — Tangram's 7 pieces form a deceptively rich constraint space — each piece has multiple valid orientations and positions. The fit probability overlay reveals which pieces geometrically could fill each remaining region, turning spatial intuition into informed placement. Area matching alone eliminates most candidates; shape analysis narrows further.
- `SIM-024 territory-dice-prob` — Dicewars (2005) popularized dice-stack territory games where luck dominates. The probability overlay reveals the hidden math: attacking 6 dice vs 2 dice isn't just "probably good" — it's 98.8% certain victory. By making these probabilities visible, the game transforms from gambling into informed risk management. This is exactly what expected-value calculations do in AI decision-making: turn uncertainty into quantified risk.
- `SIM-025 merchant-trade` — Taipan (1982) challenged players to buy low and sell high across Asian ports. The profit optimization overlay reveals the mathematical structure hiding beneath: price differentials, optimal routes, and expected returns per voyage. This is linear programming applied to merchant gaming — the same math that powers modern supply chain optimization.
- `SIM-026 frontier-survival` — Oregon Trail's event system is a Monte Carlo simulation. Each day samples from probability distributions for weather, disease, and accidents. By making the survival forecast visible — running hundreds of simulated futures from the current state — we transform gut-feel decisions into informed risk management. The overlay answers: "Given my current supplies and pace, what are the odds I actually make it?"
- `SPT-030 darts-accuracy` — Most beginners aim for triple-20 because it's the highest single score. But a Gaussian throw distribution shows that inaccurate players have higher expected value aiming at the 19/7 region — the penalty for missing triple-20 into 1 or 5 is severe, while missing 19 still yields decent scores. The heatmap reveals optimal strategy as a function of your personal accuracy.
- `SPT-031 carrom-chain` — Carrom is a game of intuition — experienced players develop an internal model of how discs will scatter. The collision chain overlay externalizes this mental model, showing the full cascade of elastic collisions before you shoot. It transforms carrom from a dexterity game into a strategic planning puzzle — you can see exactly which discs will pocket and plan multi-collision shots like a billiards analyst.

**Era 5-6** — 5-6 (Ensemble & Deep Learning — structural stability prediction, physics simulation, soft-body dynamics)
- `PHY-009 goobridge` — World of Goo is a structural engineering problem disguised as a toy. Each goo ball placement is a decision about load distribution, and the spring-joint network must maintain structural integrity under gravity. This parallels finite element analysis in engineering and graph neural networks that predict physical system behavior from connectivity patterns.
- `SPT-012 ragdoll-run` — QWOP is a masterclass in difficulty through interface design rather than content. The game is trivially simple in concept but nearly impossible in execution because the control mapping violates all motor learning intuitions. RL agents can eventually solve it but require millions of episodes — mirroring how humans must build entirely new neural pathways.
- `PUZ-013 blockplanner` — Tetris is NP-complete. The AI overlay computes a heuristic evaluation for every possible placement: aggregate height, completed lines, holes created, bumpiness. This is the same evaluation function that AI Tetris players use — making the machine's judgment visible so humans can learn from it or disagree with it.

**Era 5-7** — 5-7 (Statistical Learning → Generative-Agentic — NLP, constraint satisfaction, Dr.Fill 2021)
- `PUZ-021 crossword` — Crossword construction is constraint satisfaction: each word must be valid AND intersecting letters must agree. Dr.Fill (Matt Ginsberg, 2021) used NLP embeddings to solve crosswords at human-expert level. The puzzle teaches vocabulary, lateral thinking, and constraint reasoning simultaneously.
- `ADV-008 explorermap` — Zelda's overworld is an information-gathering problem. Each unexplored room could contain a key item, an enemy, or nothing. The explorer map shows what curiosity-driven RL agents compute: the expected information gain from each direction. Rooms you haven't visited have high exploration value; dead ends have zero. This is the exploration-exploitation tradeoff visualized as a dungeon map.
- `HYB-004 cardcounter` — A deck-building game is a probability system you construct during play. Each card you add changes the distribution of future hands. The card counter overlay shows what poker players and statisticians compute: P(draw) for each remaining card, expected damage/block for different play sequences, and whether your current hand is above or below expected value. This is online policy evaluation — judging your strategy while executing it.
- `PLT-012 pathsense` — Miyamoto designed Mario levels as implicit reward shaping — coin placement guides the player along the intended path without instructions. The path sense overlay makes this design intelligence visible: it shows where the designer wants you to go, which jumps are risky, and where death is most likely. This is the reward landscape of the level, made legible.
- `PUZ-015 march-brain` — Lemmings is a task allocation problem: assign limited behaviors to autonomous agents to route them from entrance to exit. The AI overlay shows the optimal assignment — which lemmings should dig, build, or block, and where. This is the same multi-agent task allocation that warehouse robots and delivery drones solve. David Jones invented agent programming as a puzzle mechanic in 1991.
- `SCR-012 bullettime` — Bullet hell demands real-time trajectory prediction for hundreds of objects simultaneously. The overlay shows the survival topology: safe corridors between bullet streams, convergence points where bullet paths intersect (death zones), and the probability of survival for each region. Expert danmaku players compute this intuitively — the overlay makes their spatial reasoning visible.
- `SIM-011 pareto` — Civilization's genius is that no single metric tells you if you're winning. Military strength, economic output, scientific progress, and diplomatic standing are all valuable but competing objectives. The Pareto overlay shows the tradeoff frontier — the set of non-dominated strategies where improving one objective requires sacrificing another. This is multi-objective RL (MORL) made visible.
- `SPT-009 flowstate` — Csikszentmihalyi's flow theory says optimal experience occurs when challenge matches skill — too easy breeds boredom, too hard breeds anxiety. The flow overlay visualizes this in real-time: your accuracy rate (skill proxy) vs note density (challenge proxy). When you're in the flow channel, the AI maintains difficulty. When you drift out, it adjusts. This is the same dynamic difficulty adjustment that modern games use — making the AI a collaborator in your experience.

**Era 6** — 6 (Deep Learning Dawn — pattern matching, anomaly detection)
- `ADV-009 border-check` — Papers, Please is anomaly detection in human form. The player acts as a classifier — scanning documents for discrepancies against a rule set, exactly like a trained neural network detecting fraudulent inputs. Each day adds features to the decision boundary, increasing cognitive load just as deeper networks handle higher-dimensional data.
- `ADV-013 fuzzy-quest` — Chuchel represents a shift from puzzle-solving to comedic interaction — every click produces a reaction, and the game rewards curiosity with humor. The design language is closer to interactive animation than traditional adventure games, presaging AI-driven procedural comedy.
- `ADV-014 haunted-school` — Detention by Red Candle Games uses Taiwanese folklore and White Terror history to create horror that is culturally specific yet universally resonant. The breath-holding mechanic transforms the player's body into an input device — tension becomes literal. The game proves that political horror (state violence, censorship, betrayal) is more terrifying than any monster, because it actually happened.
- `ANC-008 go` — Go has 10^170 legal positions — more than atoms in the observable universe. Traditional AI (minimax) failed because the branching factor is ~250. AlphaGo combined MCTS with neural network position evaluation to defeat Lee Sedol in 2016, the most significant AI milestone since Deep Blue.
- `HYB-002 deckbuilder` — Deck-building is a meta-strategy game where you're optimizing a policy (your deck) while simultaneously executing it. Each card addition changes the probability distribution of future hands. This is online policy gradient optimization — you're adjusting your strategy based on observed rewards while the environment (enemy encounters) changes. Slay the Spire's AI uses Monte Carlo tree search for enemy behavior.
- `HYB-008 getoverit` — Getting Over It demonstrates that game AI isn't just about opponents — the terrain itself is an adversarial intelligence. Every surface is designed to punish overconfidence and reward patience. The physics simulation creates emergent difficulty that no scripted AI could match, making the mountain a perfect adversary that never cheats but always wins.
- `HYB-009 okhlos` — Okhlos demonstrates that complex crowd behavior emerges from simple rules applied to many agents — a core principle of swarm intelligence. Each citizen follows basic flocking rules (separation, alignment, cohesion toward the leader) yet the mob as a whole exhibits organic surging, scattering, and reforming behavior that feels alive.
- `HYB-010 nidhogg` — Nidhogg demonstrates how minimal combat systems (three sword heights) create deep emergent gameplay through rock-paper-scissors-like stance interactions. The tug-of-war respawn mechanic inverts the death penalty — dying is a setback, not a loss — creating sustained tension that modern competitive AI must learn to navigate.
- `HYB-012 chabudai` — Cho Chabudai Gaeshi is remarkable for making the player's emotional arc the entire game loop. The frustration-building phase is deliberately tedious — the game weaponizes boredom against the player, making the cathartic release of flipping the table genuinely satisfying. This is one of the earliest examples of a game designing for emotional payoff rather than skill mastery.
- `MAZ-014 okada` — Traffic runner games model flow dynamics and obstacle avoidance in constrained lanes. The Lagos traffic setting introduces culturally specific obstacle types and behavioral patterns that challenge AI systems trained on Western traffic assumptions.
- `PHY-007 sandbox` — Falling sand games are cellular automata with material-specific rules. Each pixel follows simple local rules (fall if empty below, flow sideways for liquids, rise for gases) but complex global behavior emerges — water finding its level, fire spreading through wood, plants growing toward light. This is emergence from simple rules, the same principle that drives Conway's Game of Life and neural cellular automata research.
- `PHY-008 tower` — Tower stacking is a structural engineering problem: center of mass must stay over the base. Each imperfect placement narrows the effective platform, raising the difficulty exponentially. MIT's robot block-stacking research uses the same physics reasoning — predict stability from visual observation, then act.
- `PHY-010 roll-collect` — Katamari's genius is a single recursive rule — absorb anything smaller, grow, repeat. This mirrors how neural networks learn hierarchical features: simple local patterns compose into increasingly complex structures. The exponential growth curve parallels how representational capacity scales with depth.
- `PLT-017 morph-platform` — Semblance inverts the platformer contract — instead of navigating fixed geometry, the player reshapes it. This mirrors generative AI's shift from consuming content to producing it; the world becomes a canvas for player expression.
- `PLT-021 endless-dash` — Cookie Run's energy-depletion mechanic reframes the auto-runner from pure reflex into resource management — the player must balance risk (collecting distant jellies) against safety, mirroring exploration-exploitation tradeoffs central to reinforcement learning.
- `SCR-014 vertical-descent` — Downwell's procedural well generation uses hand-authored room templates stitched together with random selection, creating readable yet surprising vertical layouts. The combo system — consecutive kills without landing — creates emergent risk/reward: stay airborne longer for bigger combos but risk running out of ammo and hitting enemies from the side.
- `SCR-015 dragonflight` — Dragon Flight proved that vertical shooters could dominate mobile by simplifying controls to single-touch movement with auto-fire. The gem collection and power-up meter created a satisfying feedback loop — destroy enemies to earn gems, gems fuel a devastating beam attack, which destroys more enemies. This compounding reward structure mirrors reinforcement learning's reward shaping.
- `SHT-005 royale` — Battle royale proved that a shrinking boundary was sufficient to force engagement in a large-scale game. This single spatial constraint — reducing the possibility space over time — solved the camping problem that plagued earlier multiplayer shooters and created guaranteed dramatic convergence.
- `SIM-006 lane-battle` — Clash Royale compressed the MOBA formula into 3-minute matches by making units autonomous. The player's only decisions are what to deploy, where, and when — reducing real-time strategy to pure resource management and timing. This abstraction made deep strategy accessible on mobile.
- `SIM-007 village-raid` — Clash of Clans split strategy into two asymmetric problems: defense design (offline optimization) and attack execution (real-time deployment). This separation mirrors the train/inference split in machine learning — one phase optimizes a static structure, the other executes decisions against it.
- `SIM-009 farmstead` — Farming games encode a multi-objective optimization problem: maximize profit while managing time, energy, crop rotation, and seasonal constraints. The satisfying loop of invest→wait→harvest→reinvest mirrors the explore-exploit tradeoff in reinforcement learning. Stardew Valley proved that this loop, combined with social simulation, creates one of gaming's most compelling retention mechanisms.
- `SIM-010 idle` — Idle games are pure reward-shaping experiments. The exponential growth curve with diminishing returns per upgrade models the same multi-armed bandit problem that RL agents face. Cookie Clicker's prestige system is a meta-learning reset — sacrifice current progress for a permanent multiplier, mirroring transfer learning across training runs.
- `SIM-019 recettear` — Running a shop inverts the typical RPG perspective — instead of consuming items, you must understand their perceived value to NPCs. The haggling mechanic is a repeated negotiation game where pricing signals encode information about customer budgets and preferences, a microcosm of market dynamics that modern AI explores through multi-agent economic simulations.
- `SIM-021 windrunner` — Wind Runner's dual-mode design creates a fascinating state-space bifurcation — the same player input maps to fundamentally different physics depending on ground vs sky mode. This mirrors how foundation models learn context-dependent representations where identical tokens carry different meaning based on surrounding context.
- `SPT-006 carsoccer` — Rocket League's genius was combining two solved problems — driving physics and ball physics — into an emergent whole greater than either part. The car-ball interaction creates a control problem so rich that even deep RL agents struggle to master aerial play.
- `SPT-028 rhythm-keys` — DJMAX's 6-lane layout forces bimanual coordination — left hand on S/D/F, right hand on J/K/L — creating a split-attention problem analogous to multi-head attention in transformers. The long notes add a state-tracking dimension: the model must maintain which keys are currently held while processing incoming notes.
- `SRV-005 kitchen` — Kitchen service is a real-time scheduling problem with resource constraints: multiple orders compete for limited cooking stations, ingredients, and player time. The player must solve a dynamic job-shop scheduling problem — the same NP-hard optimization problem that factory automation and logistics AI tackles. Overcooked proved that scheduling stress, when framed as cooperative chaos, is inherently fun.
- `ANC-023 go-territory` — Go's territorial evaluation was the last frontier for AI. Expert players develop intuition about which areas are "alive" or "dead" after decades of study. Monte Carlo evaluation approximates this by simulating random playouts — the heatmap makes visible what masters see intuitively.
- `FGT-009 teeworlds-momentum` — Grappling hooks in games encode Newtonian mechanics as player-facing puzzles. The swing arc is a pendulum problem, the release point is a projectile motion calculation, and chaining swings is an optimization problem over a series of ballistic trajectories. The momentum overlay makes these physics computations visible — showing the same math that spacecraft use for gravity assists.
- `PHY-013 roll-growth` — Category 1 AI-native prototype. The overlay reveals exponential growth dynamics: green glow on collectible objects, yellow on almost-reachable ones with exact deficit shown, and a projection of total size if all available objects are gathered. Makes the implicit growth curve explicit.
- `PHY-014 tower-stability` — Category 1 AI-native prototype. The overlay renders what a structural analysis system computes each frame: center of mass trajectory, moment arms, collapse probability, and optimal placement zones. Same tower-stacking mechanics as PHY-008 — an engineering analysis lens added on top.
- `RPG-011 dungeon-loot-ai` — Diablo's loot system is a weighted random variable distribution — each kill is a sample from a probability table. Players intuit these probabilities through play, building mental models of drop rates. This overlay makes the hidden distribution explicit, showing the expected vs observed loot frequencies.

**Era 6-7** — 6-7 (Deep Learning / Agentic — post-2012)
- `FIX-002 ai-escalation` — Where Space Invaders found its difficulty curve by accident, intentional tension management uses real-time performance signals to seek the flow channel — maintaining challenge without overwhelming. This is Csikszentmihalyi's flow theory (1990) operationalized as code, 12 years after Space Invaders accidentally discovered it.
- `PHY-002 safety-map` — Category 1 AI-native prototype. The heatmap renders what a safety-constrained RL agent evaluates each frame: trajectory threat zones, safe corridors, and how the exploration-exploitation tradeoff materializes spatially. Same mechanics as PHY-001 — a second lens added on top.
- `TRP-002 risk-heatmap` — The heatmap makes visible what the skilled player intuits: optimal entry windows based on Qix position and trajectory. This is an advantage function A(s,a) = Q(s,a) - V(s) applied to spatial game theory — the difference between "what you'd get" and "what you expect." Formalized in RL in the 1990s; Qix players discovered it empirically in 1981.
- `SRV-003 flowbar` — The breakthrough over Tapper is the feedback loop: serve faster → attract more customers → environment becomes harder. Customers have memory (regulars return) and social behavior (impatient customers drive away newcomers). The bar becomes a living system. This is what an LLM-era agent designer adds: the environment is no longer static wave scripting — it tracks you and responds.

**Era 7** — 7 (Generative Age — emergent narrative through genre transformation)
- `ADV-010 survival-text` — A Dark Room pioneered genre-reveal as a narrative device. The game's AI is its pacing algorithm — it decides when to surface new mechanics based on accumulated state, creating a personalized difficulty curve. Each genre layer (idle, management, exploration, combat) emerges from the same state machine, proving that genre boundaries are artificial constructs the player imposes, not inherent to game systems.
- `ADV-011 cafe-chat` — Coffee Talk pioneered barista-as-therapist gameplay where the act of making drinks is a dialogue mechanic. The game's AI is its branching conversation system — drink choices reshape character arcs, proving that listening and serving are forms of agency. Toge Productions (Jakarta) brought Southeast Asian warmth to the visual novel genre.
- `ADV-012 one-minute-quest` — Minit weaponizes the roguelike death loop as a puzzle mechanic. The 60-second timer transforms a Zelda-like world into a constraint satisfaction problem — each life is a hypothesis about which path to take, which item to grab, which shortcut to unlock. Persistent progress across deaths turns death from failure into iteration. The Dutch team (Nijman from Vlambeer) brought arcade intensity to contemplative exploration.
- `ADV-016 phone-spy` — Replica by SOMI transforms the phone itself into a surveillance apparatus. The player becomes a willing participant in state surveillance — every tap, every message read, every photo opened is logged. The game weaponizes the most intimate device in modern life (the smartphone) to make the player feel complicit. This is interaction design as political critique: the UI is the argument.
- `HYB-003 autobattler` — Auto-battlers separate strategy from execution. The player designs a system (unit composition and positioning) then watches it execute autonomously. This is the core challenge of AI alignment: specifying objectives and constraints rather than actions. The emergent combat behavior from simple unit rules mirrors how complex behavior emerges from simple agent specifications.
- `HYB-013 skul` — Skul inverts the roguelite power fantasy by making the player character disposable — your body is a skeleton, power comes from wearing different skulls. This modular identity system creates emergent class-switching strategy reminiscent of job systems but in real-time combat. The Korean indie scene produced several globally successful roguelites by combining accessible action with deep systemic depth.
- `PLT-022 hex-strategy` — MO:Astray's body-possession mechanic mirrors how foundation models adapt to different tasks by switching context. The slime is a general-purpose agent that gains specialized abilities through the bodies it inhabits — much like a single model fine-tuned for different domains.
- `PLT-023 rogue-dungeon` — Dungreed's weapon-switching combat creates emergent combo systems from simple rule interactions — each weapon has distinct timing, range, and damage, and the player discovers optimal chains through experimentation. This mirrors how foundation models compose learned primitives into novel outputs.
- `PUZ-017 word-guess` — Optimal Wordle play maximizes expected information gain per guess. 3Blue1Brown showed the best opening word eliminates the most possibilities on average. This IS the same entropy maximization that decision trees and active learning use — the game teaches information theory through play.
- `PUZ-024 babaisyou` — Baba Is You inverts the typical puzzle paradigm. Instead of solving within fixed rules, you modify the rules themselves. The game's sentences form a tiny programming language — noun IS property — where the player is both programmer and avatar. This creates a meta-puzzle space where the solution is often to redefine the problem.
- `PUZ-029 cincopaus` — Cinco Paus inverts the traditional roguelike information paradigm. Where most games reward knowledge accumulation, Brough's design makes uncertainty the core mechanic. Each run generates fresh mysteries — the AI system that assigns abilities to wands creates a unique puzzle space where experimentation IS the gameplay, not preparation for it.
- `RPG-010 time-crystal-rpg` — Cris Tales' simultaneous past/present/future display is a spatial visualization of temporal branching — the player sees causality rendered in real-time across three panels. This UI innovation transforms time manipulation from an abstract mechanic into a visceral, visual experience. Colombia's first major international game.
- `SHT-008 cell-absorb` — Agar.io demonstrated that profound emergent complexity arises from trivial rules: bigger eats smaller. No scripted alliances, no designed strategies — yet players spontaneously developed teaming, splitting attacks, virus usage, and bait tactics. The game is a petri dish for emergent behavior, mirroring how simple reward signals in AI produce complex strategies.
- `SIM-017 unbox-sort` — Unpacking inverts game design conventions by removing instructions, scores, and timers. The player discovers meaning through the spatial grammar of everyday objects. Each room is a puzzle whose solution is empathy — understanding where a person would put their things. This is procedural rhetoric through placement, a design philosophy that AI systems can learn from: sometimes the most powerful interaction is the gentlest.
- `PUZ-040 word-entropy` — Every Wordle guess is an experiment. The entropy overlay reveals how much information each guess extracts from the possibility space. Optimal play means choosing the word that, on average, eliminates the most possibilities — the word with the highest expected information gain in bits. 3Blue1Brown showed that SALET and CRANE are near-optimal openers because they partition the 2,315 answer space most evenly across color patterns.
- `SHT-011 royale-zone` — Battle royale games hide their most critical information: where the zone will shrink next. Players develop intuitions about zone placement based on map geometry and past experience. The overlay makes the prediction model explicit — showing probability distributions for the next circle center, player density heatmaps, and the optimal position that balances safety from both the zone and other players.
- `NEW-001 thread` — Geometry-under-pressure predates AI-assisted design. An AI designer would have added real-time threat assessment and trail optimization layers, externalizing the visceral loop the player currently feels internally.
- `NEW-002 echo` — Echo introduces temporal self-collaboration — the player's past actions become autonomous agents that replay deterministically. This transforms single-player into asynchronous multiplayer with yourself, creating a planning problem where you must design sequences that work in concert across time.
- `NEW-003 pulse` — Pulse separates rhythm gameplay from music — the rhythm IS the physics engine. Every element operates on phase cycles: walls expand and contract, gravity oscillates, platforms appear and vanish. The player must internalize the world's heartbeat and move in sync with it, creating a meditative flow state without any audio cues.
- `NEW-004 fold` — Fold transforms the game surface itself into the primary interaction object. Instead of moving through space, you reshape space. This is topology as gameplay — the player manipulates the manifold that the game exists on, a concept borrowed from mathematical topology where surfaces can be continuously deformed.
- `NEW-005 swarm` — Swarm dissolves the concept of a player character. You are not controlling an entity — you are influencing a collective. Each particle follows simple boids rules (separation, alignment, cohesion) but the player modulates these parameters in real-time, creating a new interaction paradigm where the "self" is distributed and emergent.
- `NEW-006 decay` — Decay makes the second law of thermodynamics playable. The world tends toward disorder — platforms crumble, walls thin, structures collapse. But entropy is not purely destructive: collapsing walls reveal hidden passages, crumbling floors expose underground routes. The player must surf the wave of entropy, using destruction strategically while spending limited energy to preserve critical paths.
- `NEW-007 signal` — Signal reimagines the player as a physical phenomenon rather than an entity. You are a wave — you propagate, reflect, attenuate, and interfere. This creates gameplay from physics that games have never used as a primary mechanic: signal processing, wave interference, and frequency modulation become verbs.
- `NEW-008 catalyst` — Catalyst inverts the fundamental game assumption that the player acts ON the world. Instead, the player acts on the RULES of the world. You change whether fire attracts or repels water, whether gravity pulls or pushes, whether enemies chase or flee. This is meta-gameplay — playing the system rather than playing within it.
- `NEW-009 negative` — Negative Space inverts the figure-ground relationship of every game ever made. You are not a thing — you are the absence of a thing. Objects don't avoid you; they fall into you. You don't collect items; you consume space. This philosophical inversion creates gameplay from the concept of emptiness having agency.
- `NEW-010 tether` — Tether makes constraint satisfaction visible and tangible. Every node pulls on every connected node through elastic bonds. Moving one thing moves everything connected to it. This transforms spatial puzzles into graph theory problems — the player manipulates topology (connections) as much as geometry (positions).
- `NEW-011 bloom` — Bloom turns cellular automata from a mathematical curiosity into competitive gameplay. Two colonies compete for territory through emergent growth patterns. The player doesn't control individual cells — they set initial conditions and watch life unfold. Strategy emerges from understanding which patterns are stable, which grow, and which die, making this a game of systems literacy.
- `NEW-012 shadow` — Shadow creates a dual-entity puzzle where both entities are controlled indirectly through physics. The character moves directly, but the shadow is controlled by repositioning the light source. The shadow can interact with objects the character cannot reach, creating a cooperative puzzle between a being and its own shadow — a metaphor for conscious and unconscious action.
- `NEW-013 drift` — Drift removes the most fundamental assumption of game design: that the player controls the character. Instead, you control the ENVIRONMENT. By placing directional currents, you create a vector field that carries your character passively. This inverts the player-world relationship — you program the world to move the player, not the other way around.
- `NEW-014 fractal` — Fractal makes scale a gameplay dimension. The world is self-similar — zoom in and you find the same patterns repeated smaller. A wall at macro scale is made of smaller walls at micro scale. Moving a block at the small scale shifts the corresponding structure at all larger scales, creating cross-scale causality that has never been a game mechanic.
- `NEW-015 membrane` — Membrane uses the player's body as the primary tool — not a rigid character but a deformable boundary. The membrane's shape determines its function: stretched thin to reach distant nutrients, compressed to resist toxins, extended into pseudopods to engulf targets. Cell division as a game mechanic transforms a single-entity game into a multi-entity management challenge.
- `NEW-016 inversion` — Inversion requires the player to think in two states simultaneously. Every move must be valid in BOTH the normal and inverted worlds. This creates a unique cognitive challenge — dual-state planning — that has no direct parallel in game history. The player must find paths that work in two contradictory realities.
- `NEW-017 ripple` — Ripple makes wave interference tangible. Players must understand constructive and destructive interference intuitively — timing clicks so wave peaks align to amplify effects, or canceling waves to create calm zones. This turns wave physics from a textbook concept into a felt experience.
- `NEW-018 symbiont` — Symbiont creates two entities with opposite physical properties connected by an elastic bond. Heavy sinks, light floats. Heavy breaks floors, light reaches ceilings. Together they form a complete system — neither can solve the puzzle alone. This models symbiotic relationships where two incomplete entities create a complete organism through cooperation.
- `NEW-019 spectrum` — Spectrum adds a new dimensional axis to 2D gameplay: frequency. Three overlapping realities exist simultaneously, each visible only at its frequency. The player must shift between them to find paths, keys, and solutions. Objects that span multiple frequencies create anchor points between realities. This models the idea of parallel realities separated not by space but by wavelength.
- `NEW-020 accrete` — Accrete inverts the character-ability relationship. In traditional games, abilities are properties of the character. In Accrete, the character IS its abilities — a shapeless accumulation whose physical form determines what it can do. Long shapes reach far. Round shapes roll. Heavy shapes break barriers. Your identity is literally constructed from what you've encountered.
- `NEW-021 mycelium` — Mycelium reimagines the player as a decentralized network organism rather than a point entity. Growth replaces movement as the primary verb. The player makes topological decisions about connectivity, redundancy, and resource flow — creating emergent optimization puzzles through biological network design.
- `NEW-022 kintsugi` — Kintsugi inverts the damage-as-punishment paradigm that dominates game design. Instead of repairing to restore, repair transforms — gold seams are MORE beautiful than the original. This creates a genuine aesthetic tension: do you repair for function or for beauty? The game makes the player an artist working against entropy, discovering that imperfection and repair can create something greater than pristine wholeness.
- `NEW-023 dialectic` — Dialectic translates philosophical reasoning into spatial mechanics. Ideas become physical objects with mass, spin, and compatibility — making abstract intellectual processes tangible. The chain-reaction system (synthesis becomes new thesis) mirrors how knowledge genuinely evolves through productive contradiction.
- `NEW-024 apophenia` — Apophenia turns the player's own pattern-recognition machinery against them. The brain is a prediction engine that over-fires — seeing faces in clouds, constellations in random stars, meaning in noise. This game makes that cognitive bias the core mechanic: every false positive degrades your perception, while patience and restraint are rewarded. The line between insight and delusion becomes the skill curve.
- `NEW-025 saudade` — Absence as a game design element inverts the standard paradigm where the world is solid by default. Here, the world is gone by default — memory is the active force that temporarily rebuilds reality. This transforms an untranslatable emotional concept into a navigable mechanic, letting players feel saudade rather than merely understanding it.
- `NEW-026 ubuntu` — Ubuntu inverts the player-as-individual paradigm. Your success is literally inseparable from everyone else's. The game mechanizes communitarian ethics: neglecting one node cascades harm through the network, while helping one cascades benefit. It asks whether Western game design's fixation on individual achievement is a design choice or a cultural bias.
- `NEW-027 palimpsest` — Palimpsest treats time not as a sequence but as a stack of transparent overlays. The player reads through history the way a scholar reads a palimpsest — all eras coexist simultaneously, each partially visible, each containing truths the others have erased. Navigation becomes an act of historical interpretation.
- `NEW-028 desire` — Desire lines reveal the gap between designed systems and actual human behavior. This game makes emergent behavior itself the primary input — the player observes autonomous agents, then responds. The feedback loop where paving changes behavior mirrors how all designed systems reshape the behavior they were built to serve.
- `NEW-029 liminal` — Threshold spaces become the only playable terrain, inverting the architectural assumption that rooms are destinations and hallways are mere connectors. Identity becomes positional — you are what you stand between. The game mechanizes Victor Turner's insight that transformation happens not in defined states but in the passage between them.
- `NEW-030 ikigai` — Ikigai transforms a philosophical diagram into spatial gameplay. The Venn diagram becomes a living system where overlaps are not static labels but dynamic zones that expand and contract based on player investment. The insight is that balance itself can be a game mechanic — not as a meter to maintain, but as a geometric relationship between competing priorities.
- `NEW-031 terroir` — Terroir dissolves the player-avatar distinction by making the player the landscape itself. Identity is expressed not through action but through character — the unique combination of soil, water, temperature, and minerals that defines what can grow. The game asks: what does your place taste like?
- `NEW-032 hygge` — Hygge inverts the fundamental assumption of game design: that more is better. Here, contentment is the score, restraint is the strategy, and the optimal state is deliberately sparse. The game rewards the player for NOT acting — for finding the minimal combination that maximizes warmth. This is anti-challenge design: the enemy is your own impulse to optimize through addition.
- `NEW-033 tsundoku` — Tsundoku mechanizes the universal tension between acquisition and comprehension. In an era of infinite information, the scarce resource is not access but attention. This game literalizes the paradox: every book you read means others pile up unread, and the pile itself becomes the enemy. Knowledge hoarding is not knowledge.
- `NEW-034 bricolage` — Bricolage inverts the engineering mindset that dominates game design. Instead of optimal tools for defined problems, the player improvises with found materials — discovering that constraint breeds creativity. The scoring system rewards lateral thinking over efficiency, making the game a playable argument for Lévi-Strauss's thesis that the bricoleur's logic is as rigorous as the engineer's.
- `NEW-035 semiotics` — Semiotics turns interpretation itself into the core gameplay verb. The gap between signifier and signified — the fact that a red arrow can mean exit, danger, or treasure depending on context — creates a puzzle space that is fundamentally linguistic rather than spatial. The player becomes a reader, and the world becomes a text that must be decoded through observation, hypothesis, and revision.
- `NEW-036 heterotopia` — Heterotopia translates Foucault's concept of "other spaces" into spatial gameplay mechanics. Each room type enforces a different logic — mirrors split agency, libraries collapse geography, cemeteries fold time — requiring the player to hold simultaneous contradictory rules. The game becomes a philosophical instrument: spaces that contain their own negation demand a form of play that is itself heterotopic.
- `NEW-037 rhizome` — Rhizome dismantles the assumption that game worlds need hierarchy, center, or direction. Navigation becomes disorientation-as-mechanic: the player must abandon spatial intuition and learn associative logic. The "map" is deliberately misleading because rhizomatic connections are non-spatial — proximity on screen does not imply connectivity, forcing the player to think topologically rather than geometrically.
- `NEW-038 abyme` — Abyme collapses the boundary between container and contained. In traditional games, the game world is a stage the player acts upon. Here, the stage contains itself — actions at one scale ripple through recursive copies, creating cross-scale causation that mirrors the strange loops of Hofstadter and the infinite regress of Borges. The player must think simultaneously at multiple levels of abstraction.
- `NEW-039 entelechy` — Entelechy inverts the standard game design assumption that the player knows what they are building. Here, each entity contains a hidden telos — a purpose the player must discover through experimentation. The act of nurturing is simultaneously an act of inquiry: applying elements is hypothesis-testing, and the entity's responses are data. This transforms Aristotle's metaphysics of potentiality and actuality into a playable loop where discovery and creation are indistinguishable.
- `NEW-040 chiaroscuro` — Chiaroscuro transforms the gradient between knowing and not-knowing into a navigable interaction zone. Just as Caravaggio used dramatic lighting to guide the viewer's eye to the emotionally charged moment, the player must learn to see through controlled partial illumination — full knowledge (light) and full ignorance (dark) are equally useless. The sweet spot of discovery lies in the dramatic edge where certainty dissolves into mystery, making Renaissance art theory into a playable mechanic.
- `NEW-041 ostranenie` — Games teach players to stop seeing — to automate perception into reflexes. Ostranenie reverses this: it systematically breaks every automation the player builds, forcing continuous re-perception. The familiar platformer becomes a site of estrangement where red no longer means danger, down no longer means down, and the player character itself becomes uncertain. This is Shklovsky's "making strange" applied to interactive systems.
- `NEW-042 lullaby` — Lullaby inverts the rhythm game — instead of escalating intensity, success means reducing stimulation. The player's skill is restraint and smoothness rather than speed and precision. The game rewards you for approaching stillness, making the win condition paradoxically about doing less.
- `NEW-043 puddle` — Puddle captures a universal childhood joy — splashing in rain — and discovers a game mechanic within it. The ripple-as-collection-tool is a novel verb: you don't touch the items directly, you create waves that bring them to you. Indirect collection through physics creates a more satisfying feedback loop than direct pickup.
- `NEW-044 blanketfort` — Blanket forts invert traditional building games — the construction material is soft, saggy, and impermanent. Success requires understanding catenary curves intuitively. The player builds not for permanence but for temporary shelter, which mirrors how children use play to create transient safe spaces.
- `NEW-045 firefly` — Firefly makes light itself the consumable resource. Unlike torch-based games where light depletes uniformly, each firefly is an independent timer creating a dynamic, heterogeneous light budget. The player must constantly acquire new light sources while spending existing ones — a beautiful resource management metaphor wrapped in childhood wonder.
- `NEW-046 toast` — Toast discovers that breakfast preparation is a natural parallel-processing challenge. Three independent timing tasks that must converge simultaneously creates cognitive load through real-world familiarity rather than abstraction. Everyone knows what burnt toast looks like — no tutorial needed.
- `NEW-047 snowball` — Snowball merges the collection phase and the creation phase of gameplay. Normally these are separate loops — gather resources, then build. Here, the gathering IS the building: the snowball is simultaneously your vehicle, your score, and your raw material. The snowman result is an emergent artwork from your navigation choices.
- `NEW-048 kite` — Kite flying is indirect control — you don't move the kite, you adjust the string, and wind does the rest. This creates a unique control feel where the player collaborates with a dynamic environment rather than fighting it. The string is simultaneously constraint and connection, limitation and lifeline.
- `NEW-049 treehouse` — Treehouse adds a living reward to stacking games — birds nesting in your creation. This transforms building from abstract score into nurturing: you're not stacking for points, you're creating a home. The shift from mechanical to emotional feedback changes how the player relates to their construction.
- `NEW-050 seedling` — Seedling makes the player a caretaker rather than a hero. The plant grows on its own schedule — you can only provide conditions. This asymmetric agency (you prepare, nature acts) creates a uniquely gentle tension where patience is as important as action.
- `NEW-051 paperfold` — Origami is a constraint-satisfaction puzzle in physical space — each fold constrains future possibilities while revealing the shape. Paperfold makes this visible: the player sees the solution emerging from their choices, creating a satisfying reveal where the answer was hidden inside the flat sheet all along.
- `NEW-052 carousel` — Carousel turns a merry-go-round into a timing-matching puzzle. The circular motion creates a natural clock — opportunities come around again but conditions change. Speed control adds a second axis: you're managing both WHEN (timing) and HOW FAST (pacing) simultaneously. It's resource scheduling on a wheel.
- `NEW-053 mittens` — Mittens combines catching (action) with matching (puzzle) and adds wind (chaos). The basket capacity limit creates a memory-management challenge — holding mismatches costs capacity. The player must decide in real-time whether to catch a mitten hoping its pair comes soon, or skip it to save basket space.
- `NEW-054 campfire` — Campfire discovers that maintaining a RANGE is more interesting than reaching a MAXIMUM. Most games reward going higher — more points, more power. Here, the sweet spot is a gentle zone that requires constant attention. The animals are living feedback indicators, making the abstract heat value tangible and emotionally rewarding.
- `NEW-055 lighthouse` — Lighthouse inverts the typical player-object relationship. You don't control the ships — you control the environment (light) and ships respond. This makes the player a guardian rather than an actor, creating a protective emotional dynamic rarely found in games. The tension comes from not being able to help everyone at once.
- `NEW-056 paperboat` — Paperboat makes the vehicle fragile and temporary — a paper boat in water is inherently doomed. This creates a gentle ticking clock (sogginess) that feels natural rather than arbitrary. The player isn't fighting enemies; they're collaborating with physics to extend a small, beautiful moment.
- `NEW-057 starmap` — Starmap adds temporal availability to connect-the-dots — you can see all the stars but can only interact with them when they're bright. This creates a rhythm of observation and action: wait, watch, click. The twinkling transforms a simple puzzle into a meditative dance with celestial timing.
- `NEW-058 bakery` — Bakery combines creative expression with pattern matching under time pressure. The grading system must fuzzy-match freehand drawings against templates — a computer vision problem solved here through spatial proximity scoring. Players experience the joy of creation while the game quietly evaluates similarity.
- `NEW-059 birdnest` — Birdnest creates a complete lifecycle arc — build, incubate, nurture — as a game. The emotional payoff (hatching babies) is earned through accumulated small acts of care. This differs from most games where reward is immediate; here, delayed gratification IS the design, and the investment makes the payoff deeply satisfying.
- `NEW-060 bubblebath` — Bubblebath reimagines the shrinking-arena concept (battle royale's zone) as a draining bathtub — the same spatial pressure mechanic but rendered through universal childhood experience. The drain is the antagonist, the water is the play space, and the duck is the player. Familiar anxiety made adorable.
- `NEW-061 musicbox` — Musicbox transforms music appreciation into a spatial puzzle. Notes are physical objects placed on a cylinder — pitch becomes height, timing becomes position. The player doesn't need to read music; they see the melody as a landscape of pegs and fill in the gaps intuitively. Music theory becomes tactile pattern-matching.
- `NEW-062 graviton` — The game applies variable-ratio reinforcement through near-miss orbits and zen flow through hypnotic trail patterns. The physics are real (inverse-square gravity) but the aesthetics transform math into art. Each trajectory is unique — the player becomes a composer of motion.
- `NEW-063 chromashift` — Color-matching is instinctive — no learning curve needed. The constant switching creates a rhythm that induces flow state. The screen becomes a rave of color. Death is always from split-second color confusion — creating genuine "one more try" motivation.
- `NEW-064 timeshadow` — You ARE the difficulty generator. Every safe path you take NOW becomes an obstacle you must avoid in 5 seconds. The game creates exponentially growing complexity from zero rules. After 30 seconds, you're dodging 6 ghosts of yourself. The cognitive load of planning for your future self while dodging your past selves is uniquely mind-bending.
- `NEW-065 bloomgarden` — The game has no failure state. Beauty IS the reward. Each flower is procedurally unique — different petal count, colors, shapes, stem curves. The garden you grow is yours alone. This targets the emotional need for creation without consequence — play as meditation.
- `NEW-066 pendulum` — The release timing creates a micro-skill with infinite mastery ceiling. Perfect release angle sends you soaring; bad timing drops you. The pendulum physics feel incredible when chained — like being Spider-Man with one button. The game targets the "flow through physics mastery" pleasure.
- `NEW-067 dualcontrol` — Dualcontrol externalizes the cognitive phenomenon of divided attention. The same input drives two characters in a mirrored world — one walks on floors, the other on ceilings. The player must think in two spatial frames simultaneously, discovering that some movements help one character while hindering the other. The puzzle becomes a negotiation between two selves sharing one brain.
- `NEW-068 chainblast` — Chainblast distills strategy into a single decision — where to click. The entire game resolves from one action, yet that action requires reading the spatial topology of the field. Near-misses (one orb short) create an irresistible retry loop. The escalating pitch of chained explosions transforms optimization into music.
- `NEW-069 colorflood` — Colorflood distills optimization into its purest form. Each move is trivially simple — pick a color — but the consequences cascade through the grid in ways that reward spatial reasoning and planning. The "just one more move" addiction emerges from the gap between understanding the mechanic instantly and mastering the strategy over hundreds of plays.
- `NEW-070 wordweave` — Wordweave turns the quiet act of vocabulary recall into a physical sprint. The chain constraint — each word must start with the last letter of the previous — creates a branching decision tree that narrows under time pressure. Players discover their vocabulary has topology: some letters are hubs (E, S, T) while others are dead ends (X, Z). The game reveals the hidden geography of language.
- `NEW-071 orbiter` — Orbiter transforms orbital mechanics into intuitive play. The player doesn't need to understand Kepler's laws — they feel them through the arc of their satellite. Too fast and it escapes into the void; too slow and it spirals into the planet. The sweet spot — a stable elliptical orbit — emerges naturally as the most beautiful trajectory.
- `NEW-072 mirrorbound` — Mirrorbound forces players to think in symmetry. Every movement has a consequence on the opposite side of the screen. The cognitive load of planning two paths simultaneously creates a puzzle-like quality within an action framework. The mirror is not an enemy — it is you. Learning to protect it is learning to think beyond yourself.
- `NEW-073 stackphysics` — Stackphysics asks what Tetris would be if gravity were real. Blocks don't snap to a grid — they rest on surfaces, lean against edges, and topple when center of mass shifts past support. The tension of a wobbling tower about to collapse creates drama that no grid-based game can match. Every placement is a physics negotiation.
- `NEW-074 weavethrough` — Weavethrough reframes dodging as dance. Traditional bullet-hell games punish proximity; here, proximity IS the game. Grazing rewards the player for flirting with danger, turning evasion into expression. The geometric patterns are simultaneously obstacles and art — the player's trail weaves through them like thread through a loom, creating a unique tapestry each run.
- `NEW-075 onelineall` — Onelineall distills puzzle satisfaction to its purest form. There is no timer, no score, no enemy. Just dots and the challenge of visiting them all with one continuous line. The reward is entirely internal — the aha moment when you see the path, and the rainbow celebration when you complete it. Completionism as meditation.
- `NEW-076 bouncewall` — Bouncewall distills strategy to its purest form. With only 5 walls and a ceaselessly bouncing ball, every placement is a commitment. The game asks not "can you solve this?" but "can you solve this elegantly?" It transforms physics into a puzzle of foresight, where the optimal solution often requires predicting trajectories several bounces deep.
- `NEW-077 alchemist` — Alchemist taps into the universal human drive to experiment. Every pair of elements whispers "what if?" and the player cannot resist trying. The dopamine hit of a new discovery — the flash, the chime, the counter ticking up — creates a compulsion loop that feels like genuine curiosity rather than grinding. Discovery IS the gameplay.
- `NEW-078 beatjump` — Beatjump dissolves the boundary between music and movement. Instead of pressing buttons to match visual prompts, the player's physical navigation IS the rhythm game. Platforms exist only on the beat — your body learns the tempo before your mind does. The music isn't accompaniment; it's architecture.
- `NEW-079 shapemorph` — Shapemorph distills gameplay to a single binary: match or die. With only one button cycling through three states, the player's challenge is purely perceptual — recognizing the approaching shape and counting presses. At speed, the conscious counting vanishes and the response becomes instinctive. You stop thinking about shapes and start feeling them.
- `NEW-080 inktrail` — Inktrail inverts the typical maze game. Instead of navigating walls someone else built, you BUILD the walls by moving. Every step is simultaneously progress and constraint. The game becomes a meditation on commitment — each decision permanently reshapes the world, and your beautiful ink trail is both your art and your prison.
- `NEW-081 sortcatch` — Sort the Sky taps into the deeply human sorting instinct — the satisfaction of correct placement combined with the chaos of acceleration. As speed increases, deliberate categorization gives way to frantic pattern-matching, revealing the boundary between conscious classification and intuitive recognition.
- `NEW-082 gravity-paddle` — GravityPong replaces Pong's predictable linear trajectories with orbital curves. The gravity well transforms every rally into a unique celestial dance — the ball swoops, arcs, and slingshots around the central star. Players must read curved paths instead of straight lines, making spatial intuition more important than reflexes. The result feels like table tennis played on the surface of a neutron star.
- `NEW-083 puzzlefight` — PuzzleFight asks what happens when abstract puzzle mastery becomes embodied violence. Each cleared line is simultaneously a spatial achievement and a punch thrown. The player exists in two frames at once — the meditative flow of Tetris and the aggressive urgency of a fighting game. Combos reward sustained focus with escalating power, creating a feedback loop where puzzle skill literally hits harder.
- `NEW-084 stealthgarden` — StealthGarden fuses two genres that seem incompatible — stealth tension and pastoral calm. The result is surprisingly natural: gardening has always been about timing (seasons, weather, patience), and stealth is about timing too (patrol gaps, safe windows). The gardener becomes a spy whose mission is beauty. Every planted seed is an act of quiet rebellion against surveillance.
- `NEW-085 rhythmcraft` — RhythmCraft fuses two loops that rarely meet — rhythm action and crafting strategy. The rhythm phase is the gathering step; the crafting phase is the spending step. But the twist is that crafted items reshape the music itself, so the player's creative choices echo back as audio feedback. The crafting loop fuels the rhythm, and the rhythm fuels the crafting.
- `NEW-086 racepuzzle` — RacePuzzle fuses the spatial planning of Sokoban with the time pressure of a racing game. The flood mechanic transforms a contemplative puzzle into a frantic race — you must think ahead while running for your life. Blocks are both tools and obstacles: push one wrong and you've sealed your fate. The fusion creates a uniquely tense experience where every move counts twice.
- `NEW-087 cardplatform` — Cardplatform dissolves the assumption that platformer verbs are free. Every jump costs a card. Every attack costs a card. Movement becomes resource management — do you burn your last jump to reach a platform, or save it for the gap ahead? The deck is your body's capability manifest, and reshuffling is rebirth. Strategy emerges from scarcity in a genre built on abundance.
- `NEW-088 towerbrawl` — Tower Brawl inverts the core tower defense mechanic. Instead of omniscient placement, you ARE the defense — one body, three lanes, never enough of you. The beat-em-up physicality transforms strategic distance into frantic proximity. Every punch is a triage decision.
- `NEW-089 bulletgarden` — Bulletgarden inverts the bullet hell relationship with projectiles. Instead of destruction, bullets become seeds of beauty. The player's survival skill directly paints a living garden — dense patterns that would terrify in Touhou instead promise lush meadows. Danger becomes generative. Graze mechanics reward proximity to peril with rarer blooms, making the most beautiful gardens emerge from the bravest play.
- `NEW-090 wrestlechess` — WrestleChess asks: what if chess captures were uncertain? By replacing deterministic capture with a skill-based wrestling minigame, every exchange becomes dramatic. A pawn CAN topple a queen if the player mashes hard enough. This injects physicality and tension into the cerebral game, making positional advantage important but never absolute.
- `NEW-091 cookingrunner` — CookingRunner fuses the frantic kitchen service genre with endless runner momentum. Instead of standing at a station, you sprint through the kitchen grabbing ingredients as they fly past. Recipe completion becomes a spatial challenge — the right flour bag is at the top lane, the eggs are in the middle. The runner format transforms cooking from methodical to kinetic, creating a breathless dash through a never-ending kitchen.
- `NEW-092 reversemaze` — ReverseMaze inverts the fundamental maze paradigm. Every maze game since Pac-Man asks you to navigate through walls. Here, empty space is the problem and walls are the solution. You don't avoid walls — you ARE the walls. The ball obeys gravity and physics; your job is architectural. The satisfaction comes from seeing your wall design work as intended — the ball bouncing exactly where you planned. It's level design as gameplay.
- `NEW-093 antigravity` — Antigravity takes the single most fundamental rule of platformers — gravity pulls down — and inverts it. The character clings to the ceiling. Spikes are above. Jumping means pushing yourself downward against your natural buoyancy. This one rule change creates total cognitive dissonance: every platformer instinct is wrong. Gaps in the ceiling are deadly (you float into the void). Safe ground is above you. The familiar becomes alien through a single parameter flip.
- `NEW-094 healershooter` — Healershooter inverts the foundational shooter mechanic. Instead of destroying, you heal. Instead of reducing enemies, you recruit them. The moral inversion — compassion as weapon — creates a deeply satisfying feedback loop where the screen fills with allies born from former foes. Strategy emerges naturally: heal the strongest first.
- `NEW-095 shrinkworld` — Shrinkworld inverts the assumption that visual clarity is constant. By degrading resolution over time, the game transforms from a simple platformer into a memory challenge. Players must internalize the level layout while they can still see it, then navigate by recall as the world dissolves into blocky abstraction. The mechanic asks: how much visual information do you actually need?
- `NEW-096 silentrhythm` — SilentRhythm inverts the fundamental assumption of rhythm games: that music leads and you follow. Here, silence is the canvas. Each accurate hit paints a note onto it. The player discovers they were always the musician — the game just provided the score. Miss a beat and hear nothing; the absence is more punishing than any penalty sound. Perfect play rewards you with a complete melody you created through precision alone.
- `NEW-097 builddestroy` — BuildDestroy inverts the relationship between designer and player. Normally the designer creates challenge and the player endures it. Here you are both. The optimal strategy is to build the hardest arena you can JUST barely survive — a moving target that teaches you about your own skill ceiling. Every round is a negotiation with yourself.
- `NEW-098 ecosystem` — Ecosystem distills ecology into its simplest interactive form. Three species with trivial rules — grow, eat, reproduce, die — produce complex emergent dynamics. The player's only tool is sunlight, an indirect lever that cascades through the food chain. You don't control life; you influence it.
- `NEW-099 paintphysics` — PaintPhysics inverts the typical physics puzzle. Instead of placing rigid objects, the player paints with colors that embody physical laws. Red paint rises like heat, blue falls like rain, green clings like moss, yellow bounces like rubber. The canvas becomes a living physics laboratory where every brushstroke triggers emergent behavior. Solutions feel creative rather than calculated.
- `NEW-100 musicterrain` — Musicterrain collapses two creative acts into one — composing music and designing levels. Every note has dual meaning: an audible pitch and a physical height. The melody IS the architecture. Players discover that pleasing melodies often create interesting terrain, and vice versa. Music theory becomes level design theory. A scale is a staircase. An arpeggio is a mountain range.
- `NEW-101 lightandshadow` — Light and Shadow inverts the typical platformer relationship with level geometry. Instead of platforms being fixed, they are ephemeral projections of light. The player must think spatially about light angles while also timing movement across platforms that exist only as long as the light shines on them. Moving the light source while standing on a light-created platform creates a delicious tension — repositioning to open the next path might erase the ground beneath your feet.
