- `NEW-102 emotionengine` — EmotionEngine asks what happens when feelings ARE mechanics. Most games treat emotion as narrative flavor — cutscenes make you sad, victories make you happy. Here, emotion is the core system. Joy literally makes you jump higher. Fear literally makes you run faster. The player must learn to harness their character's emotional responses as tools, turning vulnerability into power.
- `NEW-103 timewaves` — Timewaves explores the relationship between perception and action speed. By making time itself a spatial phenomenon — waves that sweep across the field — the game creates a rhythm of contemplation and execution. Players learn to read the temporal landscape and position themselves strategically, surfing between slow-time planning and fast-time action.
- `NEW-104 crowdsource` — Crowdsource inverts the typical player-avatar relationship. Instead of controlling one character precisely, you influence 100 imprecise agents statistically. The crowd becomes a living fluid — you can guide it but never fully control it. Emergent behavior means rebels sometimes save the group and leaders sometimes cause stampedes.
- `NEW-105 memorygame` — A Game That Remembers You inverts the player-game relationship. Most games ask you to learn their patterns. This game learns YOUR patterns — and punishes predictability. The only way to win is to become unpredictable, to break the habits you didn't know you had. It is a mirror held up to muscle memory itself.
- `NEW-106 time-loop` — Deathloop inverts gaming's most fundamental assumption: that death is failure. Here, death is the only way to reshape the world. The player must overcome a lifetime of conditioning that says "don't die" and instead learn to die strategically — in the right place, at the right time, in the right order. Each death is an investment, not a loss. The puzzle is figuring out WHERE to sacrifice yourself. Death becomes creation.
- `NEW-107 pixelerosion` — Pixelerosion asks what happens when the medium itself dies. Most games punish the player; this game punishes itself. The world decays regardless of skill — platforms crumble, colors drain, sprites dissolve. You're not fighting enemies; you're racing against entropy. The haunting final moments, where you navigate abstract shapes from memory, create an emotional resonance no traditional game mechanic can achieve.
- `NEW-108 sharedscore` — SharedScore transforms the ephemeral arcade experience into something with weight. Every bullet fired, every death suffered, echoes forward through time. The persistent score creates a relationship between your past, present, and future selves — a negotiation across sessions about risk, skill, and trust.
- `NEW-109 metabreaker` — Metabreaker inverts the player-game relationship. Normally the HUD is sacrosanct UI chrome — untouchable, trustworthy, separate from play. Here, the HUD IS the puzzle. Every element you assumed was read-only is actually interactive. The game teaches you to question interfaces themselves, to poke at boundaries, to see UI as content. Destruction becomes the most creative act.
- `NEW-110 nothing` — Nothing interrogates what a game IS by withholding it. The player stares at void, waits, and watches creation unfold. The reveal — that it was always a game, just waiting to exist — transforms patience into wonder. Each replay accelerates, compressing cosmogenesis. The game creates itself.
- `NEW-111 youaretheai` — You Are The AI inverts the entire player-character relationship. Instead of controlling the avatar, you tune the parameters that govern its autonomous behavior. The frustration of watching your agent fail — and the eureka of finding the right combination — mirrors the actual experience of training ML models. The game IS the meta-game.
- `NEW-112 manifold` — Manifold weaponizes the gap between Euclidean intuition and toroidal reality. Players expect straight lines to stay straight, but the twist parameter turns every path into a spiral. The trail visualization is the teaching tool — you literally see your assumptions break. Understanding the topology IS the puzzle, not a side effect of it.
- `NEW-113 tesselate` — Tesselate makes the mathematics of plane tiling tangible. Instead of memorizing which regular polygons tile the plane, players discover it through evolving shapes — each placement subtly warps the next piece, forcing intuitive adaptation. The game teaches that tessellation is not about perfection but about continuous adjustment.
- `NEW-114 fieldlines` — Fieldlines transforms electrostatics into a spatial puzzle. The player navigates as a charged particle constrained to invisible rails — the electric field lines between charges. By placing new charges, the player literally reshapes the topology of space, creating bridges and detours. Physics becomes level design.
- `NEW-115 waveinterference` — WaveInterference transforms a fundamental physics phenomenon into spatial puzzle architecture. The interference pattern — bright constructive nodes where waves align, dark destructive nulls where they cancel — becomes a living landscape the player must shape by tuning frequencies. Physics becomes level design.
- `NEW-116 voronoi` — Voronoi transforms computational geometry into intuitive spatial play. The tessellation — normally a dry mathematical construct — becomes a living maze of bouncing walls. Players don't need to understand the math; they simply drag dots and watch the walls reshape. The connection between point placement and boundary geometry becomes visceral rather than academic.
- `NEW-117 attractor` — Attractor transforms the Lorenz system from a mathematical curiosity into a precision sport. The player doesn't control the particle — they set initial conditions and watch deterministic chaos unfold. The butterfly effect becomes visceral when a 0.01 change in Z sends your trajectory to the opposite lobe. Success requires developing intuition for a system that defies intuition.
- `NEW-118 resonance` — Resonance transforms a physics classroom concept into visceral gameplay. Every object has a secret — its natural frequency — and you find it not through logic but through feel. The vibration builds, the glow intensifies, and the shattering is deeply satisfying. You become a human spectrum analyzer, sweeping through the frequency space with your body.
- `NEW-119 tensegrity` — Tensegrity transforms structural engineering into intuitive play. Rigid struts float in a web of elastic cables — compression islands in a sea of tension. The player discovers that stability emerges not from brute stacking but from balanced forces. Every successful structure is a lesson in how tension and compression cooperate.
- `NEW-120 fluidrouter` — FluidRouter transforms ratio mathematics into physical intuition. Instead of calculating 60/40 splits abstractly, players watch blue fluid divide at T-junctions and adjust valves until the visible flow matches targets. Engineering becomes aesthetic — you see the math flowing through your pipes.
- `NEW-121 harmonograph` — Harmonograph turns physics into art. Two pendulums — one for X, one for Y — combine to trace Lissajous figures. The player adjusts frequency ratios, phase, and damping to match target patterns. Simple ratios produce elegant curves (1:1 circle, 1:2 figure-8), while complex ratios create intricate rosettes. The audible harmony of two tones mirrors the visual harmony of the curve.
- `NEW-122 springmesh` — Springmesh turns wave physics into a tangible puzzle. By placing anchors and heavy masses, the player sculpts how waves travel through a connected mesh. Standing waves, resonance, waveguides, and splitters emerge naturally from Hooke's law and Verlet integration — no abstraction needed.
- `NEW-123 cellularengine` — CellularEngine inverts the usual relationship between player and game. Instead of playing within rules, you design the rules themselves. The challenge is to think about emergence — what simple local interactions produce complex global behavior? You become a physicist designing laws of nature.
- `NEW-124 sortmachine` — Sortmachine transforms abstract algorithm design into spatial engineering. A sorting network is normally a diagram in a textbook — here it becomes a machine you build, watch, and debug. Numbers flow like balls through pipes, comparators are physical gates that swap. You see WHY bubble sort needs so many comparisons and WHY optimal networks are elegant. Algorithm complexity becomes tangible.
- `NEW-125 boolcircuit` — BoolCircuit transforms abstract Boolean algebra into tangible spatial construction. Logic gates become physical objects you wire together — truth tables become observable signal flows. The satisfaction of watching yellow pulses propagate through a correct circuit bridges the gap between symbolic math and intuitive engineering.
- `NEW-126 entropy` — Entropy turns the second law of thermodynamics into a gameplay tension. Every deliberate move toward order simultaneously introduces chaos elsewhere. The player experiences the fundamental asymmetry of physics: disorder is easy, order is hard. Winning requires accepting imperfection — creating local order while the universe trends toward randomness.
- `NEW-127 compression` — Compression turns data compression into a reflex game. The player becomes a living LZ77 algorithm, scanning a streaming sequence for repeating patterns and replacing them with compact symbols. It makes the invisible work of compression visceral — you feel the buffer pressure, the relief of a good match, the panic when patterns slip past unnoticed.
- `NEW-128 graphwalk` — Graphwalk turns Euler's 1736 Königsberg bridge problem into a survival game. The player must intuitively discover that Eulerian paths require exactly 0 or 2 odd-degree nodes. Each level is guaranteed solvable, but finding the path requires spatial planning — which edge to use NOW so you don't strand yourself later. Abstract mathematics becomes visceral decision-making.
- `NEW-129 pidcontroller` — PID Controller transforms a foundational engineering concept into visceral gameplay. The three gains become intuitive: P is how hard you react, I is how stubborn you are about past mistakes, D is how cautious you are about the future. The ball's wobble, overshoot, and oscillation are the textbook diagrams come alive — no equations needed, just feel.
- `NEW-130 neuralplay` — NeuralPlay strips away the abstraction of machine learning frameworks and forces you to BE the optimizer. By manually adjusting weights and watching the agent succeed or fail, you viscerally understand what gradient descent does — and why it sometimes gets stuck. The game IS backpropagation, performed by a human brain.
- `NEW-131 statemachine` — Statemachine makes the invisible visible. Every program is a state machine, but we hide that behind text. Here the FSM diagram IS the program — circles are states, arrows are transitions, labels are logic. Watching your automaton execute is watching your own reasoning play out step by step.
- `NEW-132 gradient` — Gradient turns the abstract mathematics of optimization into visceral physical play. The player IS a gradient descent algorithm — feeling the pull of local minima, building momentum to escape, blindly searching for the global optimum. The fog of war mirrors the algorithm's limited local information. Every stuck moment teaches why optimization is hard.
- `NEW-133 lsystem` — L-systems reveal how staggering complexity emerges from trivial rules. A single rewriting rule iterated five times can produce a fractal snowflake, a branching tree, or a space-filling curve. The player doesn't draw — they program growth, discovering that nature's most intricate forms are just short sentences in a recursive grammar.
- `NEW-134 reactiondiffusion` — Reaction-diffusion transforms Turing's 1952 morphogenesis paper into a living canvas. The Gray-Scott model produces astonishing variety from just two parameters — spots, stripes, labyrinthine corridors, pulsing mitosis. The player doesn't solve equations; they sculpt emergence by nudging rates, watching order crystallize from chaos. Mathematics becomes gardening.
- `NEW-135 lifeengineer` — Life Engineer flips Conway's Game of Life from observation to engineering. Instead of watching patterns evolve, you must design initial conditions that produce specific outcomes. This transforms a mathematical curiosity into a puzzle game where emergence itself is the mechanism you must master.
- `NEW-136 particleswarm` — Particle Swarm Optimization is a computational intelligence technique inspired by bird flocking. Here it becomes a game of tuning emergent behavior — the player doesn't control any particle directly, only the rules that govern them all. The entertainment IS the emergent behavior: watching 50 dots converge, scatter, orbit, and hunt. Each landscape demands different parameter balance.
- `NEW-137 fractalzoom` — FractalZoom transforms the Mandelbrot set from a passive visualization into an active exploration game. The infinite self-similar structure becomes a world to navigate, and pattern recognition becomes the core mechanic. Mathematics itself is the content — no sprites, no assets, just z = z² + c rendered as an infinite landscape of spirals, seahorses, and miniature copies of the whole set.
- `NEW-138 quantumcoin` — QuantumCoin distills quantum computing into its most tangible form. A qubit's probability is just a slider between two outcomes — gates nudge that slider in ways that feel counterintuitive until they click. The Z gate's invisible phase flip teaches the deepest lesson: information you can't see still changes the future. Players build intuition for superposition without ever touching the math.
- `NEW-139 phasor` — Phasor turns complex multiplication into a spatial puzzle. Each operation rotates and scales your position on the complex plane. The player doesn't need to know complex analysis — they see spirals and rotations emerge from clicking buttons. The mathematics of Euler's formula becomes intuitive geometric play.
- `NEW-140 feedback` — Feedback turns a single slider into infinite nuance. The gain parameter controls everything — responsiveness, overshoot, oscillation, stability. Players discover control theory intuitively: too little gain and the system can't keep up, too much and it tears itself apart. The sweet spot shifts with each signal type, teaching that stability is context-dependent.
- `NEW-141 ruleexplorer` — Ruleexplorer transforms computational theory into aesthetic experience. Wolfram's 256 elementary cellular automaton rules are a finite universe of emergent complexity — from dead uniformity to Turing-complete computation. By letting the player browse, rate, and curate rules, the game becomes a gallery of mathematical beauty. The classification system (Classes 1-4) gives vocabulary to what the eye already sees.
- `NEW-142 chipforge` — The entire soundtrack is procedurally synthesized from oscillator nodes and noise buffers — the same approach as ChipForge's numpy engine, ported to the browser's Web Audio API. No audio files exist; the music IS the code.
- `WLD-001 komorebi` — Komorebi proves 'game' need not mean 'contest'. The Japanese concept of light-through-leaves becomes the entire mechanic. An AI-first designer could generate infinite procedural forest compositions from this seed.

### Game-First AI Discoveries

Games that invented AI concepts before the field formalized them:

| Game | Discovered Concept | Formalized By AI (~Year) |
|------|--------------------|--------------------------|
| Pac-Man (1980) | Multi-agent behavioral policies (ghost personalities) | MARL theory (~2000) |
| Space Invaders (1978) | Emergent curriculum learning (speedup-as-fewer-enemies) | Curriculum Learning (~2015) |
| Defender (1981) | Partial observability + minimap dimensionality reduction | Practical POMDPs (~1990s) |
| Pong (1972) | Specialization over generality (Y-tracker opponent) | Narrow AI consensus (~1990s) |
| Tetris (1985) | Real-time NP-hard heuristic spatial reasoning | Active research area (ongoing) |
| Mario Bros (1985) | Reward shaping via level design | Reward shaping in RL (~1999) |
| Asteroids (1979) | Exploration-exploitation via action consequences | RL formalization (~1980s-1990s) |
| Qix (1981) | Territorial control as multi-armed bandit | Spatial bandit theory (~1985+) |
